<CENTER><H1>Problem of the Month (February 2015)</H1></CENTER>

This month we are interested in another chessboard problem.  What are the positions on an n &times; n chessboard using the fewest number of chess pieces so that each piece attacks exactly m unoccupied squares?  (We do not allow pawns.)  What are the best solutions if we insist that the positions contain at least 2 types of chess pieces? 




<P><hr><p><center><h1>ANSWERS</h1></center>

Here are the smallest known number of pieces needed, with no restrictions:<p>

<TABLE align=center cellpadding=5 border=1 bgcolor=FFFFDD bordercolor=black>
<TR align=center bgcolor=DDFFDD><TH>n \ m<TH>0<TH>1<TH>2<TH>3<TH>4<TH>5<TH>6<TH>7<TH>8<TH>9<TH>10<TH>11<TH>12<TH>13<TH>14<TH>15<TH>16<TH>17<TH>18<TH>19
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=DDFFDD>2<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=DDFFDD>3<td>1<td>2<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td><td>1
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=DDFFDD>4<td>8<td>4<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>2<td>1<td>1<td><td>1
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=DDFFDD>5<td>12<td>8<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>2<td>1<td>4<td>2<td>2<td>1<td><td>1<td><td>1
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=DDFFDD>6<td>18<td>12<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>1<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>1<td>2<td>1<td><td>1
</TABLE><p>

Here are the smallest known number of pieces needed, using at least 2 different pieces:<p>

<TABLE align=center cellpadding=5 border=1 bgcolor=EEFFFF bordercolor=black>
<TR align=center bgcolor=FFDDFF><TH>n \ m<TH>0<TH>1<TH>2<TH>3<TH>4<TH>5<TH>6<TH>7<TH>8<TH>9<TH>10<TH>11<TH>12
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>2<td>2<td>2<td>2
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>3<td>2<td>3<td>2<td>2<td>2
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>4<td>9<td>5<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>3
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>5<td>13<td>9<td>4<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>3<td>2
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>6<td>19<td>13<td>7<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>3<td>2
<TR align=center><TH bgcolor=FFDDFF>7<td> <td> <td> <td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td>2<td><td>3<td>3<td>2
</TABLE><p>

Here are the positions using the fewest known pieces, with no restrictions:<p>
